  go dc.Run(ctx, int(controllerContext.ComponentConfig.DeploymentController.ConcurrentDeploymentSyncs))\n    return nil, true, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Step 3: Controller Manager Startup**\n\nFile: `/workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`, `Run()` function:\n\n```go\nfunc Run(ctx context.Context, c *config.CompletedConfig) error {\n    // 1. Create HTTP handler and health checks\n    healthzHandler := controllerhealthz.NewMutableHealthzHandler(checks...)\n    \n    // 2. Create clients and context\n    clientBuilder, rootClientBuilder := createClientBuilders(c)\n    \n    // 3. Get all controller descriptors\n    controllerDescriptors := NewControllerDescriptors()\n    \n    // 4. Start controllers\n    run := func(ctx context.Context, controllerDescriptors map[string]*ControllerDescriptor) {\n        controllerContext, err := CreateControllerContext(ctx, c, rootClientBuilder, clientBuilder)\n        \n        // 5. Execute initialization\n        if err := StartControllers(ctx, controllerContext, controllerDescriptors, unsecuredMux, healthzHandler); err != nil {\n            // Handle error\n        }\n        \n        // 6. Start informer factories\n        controllerContext.InformerFactory.Start(stopCh)\n        controllerContext.ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory.Start(stopCh)\n    }\n    \n    // 7. Leader election loop\n    leaderElectAndRun(ctx, c, id, electionChecker, ...)\n}\n```\n\n**Step 4: StartControllers() - Individual Controller Initialization**\n\nFile: `/workspace/kubernetes--v1.32.0/cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`:\n\n```go\nfunc StartControllers(ctx context.Context, controllerCtx ControllerContext, \n    controllerDescriptors map[string]*ControllerDescriptor,\n    unsecuredMux *mux.PathRecorderMux, healthzHandler *controllerhealthz.MutableHealthzHandler) error {\n    \n    var controllerChecks []healthz.HealthChecker\n\n    // Special handling for ServiceAccountTokenController (runs first)\n    if serviceAccountTokenControllerDescriptor, ok := controllerDescriptors[names.ServiceAccountTokenController]; ok {\n        check, err := StartController(ctx, controllerCtx, serviceAccountTokenControllerDescriptor, unsecuredMux)\n        if err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n        if check != nil {\n            controllerChecks = append(controllerChecks, check)\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Start all other controllers\n    for _, controllerDesc := range controllerDescriptors {\n        if controllerDesc.RequiresSpecialHandling() {\n            continue\n        }\n        \n        check, err := StartController(ctx, controllerCtx, controllerDesc, unsecuredMux)\n        if err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n        if check != nil {\n            controllerChecks = append(controllerChecks, check)\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Register all health checks\n    healthzHandler.AddHealthChecker(controllerChecks...)\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Step 5: StartController() - Individual Controller Startup**\n\n```go\nfunc StartController(ctx context.Context, controllerCtx ControllerContext, \n    controllerDescriptor *ControllerDescriptor,\n    unsecuredMux *mux.PathRecorderMux) (healthz.HealthChecker, error) {\n    \n    logger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n    controllerName := controllerDescriptor.Name()\n\n    // 1. Check feature gates\n    for _, featureGate := range controllerDescriptor.GetRequiredFeatureGates() {\n        if !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(featureGate) {\n            return nil, nil\n        }\n    }\n\n    // 2. Skip cloud provider controllers\n    if controllerDescriptor.IsCloudProviderController() {\n        return nil, nil\n    }\n\n    // 3. Check if controller is enabled in config\n    if !controllerCtx.IsControllerEnabled(controllerDescriptor) {\n        return nil, nil\n    }\n\n    // 4. Apply startup jitter\n    time.Sleep(wait.Jitter(controllerCtx.ComponentConfig.Generic.ControllerStartInterval.Duration, ControllerStartJitter))\n\n    // 5. Call the InitFunc - THIS IS WHERE REGISTRATION HAPPENS\n    initFunc := controllerDescriptor.GetInitFunc()\n    ctrl, started, err := initFunc(klog.NewContext(ctx, klog.LoggerWithName(logger, controllerName)), controllerCtx, controllerName)\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n    if !started {\n        return nil, nil\n    }\n\n    // 6. Create default health check\n    check := controllerhealthz.NamedPingChecker(controllerName)\n\n    // 7. If controller implements Debuggable, mount debug handler\n    if debuggable, ok := ctrl.(controller.Debuggable); ok && unsecuredMux != nil {\n        if debugHandler := debuggable.DebuggingHandler(); debugHandler != nil {\n            basePath := \"/debug/controllers/\" + controllerName\n            unsecuredMux.UnlistedHandle(basePath, http.StripPrefix(basePath, debugHandler))\n        }\n    }\n\n    // 8. If controller implements HealthCheckable, use custom health check\n    if healthCheckable, ok := ctrl.(controller.HealthCheckable); ok {\n        if realCheck := healthCheckable.HealthChecker(); realCheck != nil {\n            check = controllerhealthz.NamedHealthChecker(controllerName, realCheck)\n        }\n    }\n\n    logger.Info(\"Started controller\", \"controller\", controllerName)\n    return check, nil\n}\n```\n\n### 6. **Key Integration Points**\n\n1. **Controller Discovery**: `NewControllerDescriptors()` centralizes all controller registrations\n2. **Dependency Injection**: `ControllerContext` provides clients, informers, and config\n3. **Feature Gating**: Controllers can be gated behind feature flags\n4. **Conditional Startup**: Controllers can be disabled in configuration\n5. **Health Checks**: Controllers implement `HealthCheckable` interface for `/healthz`\n6. **Debugging**: Controllers implement `Debuggable` interface for `/debug/controllers/{name}`\n7. **Leader Election**: Controllers are started only on the leader node\n8. **Jittered Startup**: Controllers start with random delays to prevent API server overload\n\n### 7. **Controller Client Access Pattern**\n\nControllers get clients via:\n```go\nclientBuilder.ClientOrDie(\"controller-name\")  // Full Kubernetes client\nclientBuilder.DiscoveryClientOrDie(\"controller-name\")  // Discovery client\n```\n\nAnd informers via:\n```go\ncontrollerContext.InformerFactory.Apps().V1().Deployments()  // Typed informer\ncontrollerContext.ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory.ForResource(gvr)  // Generic informer\n```\n\n### Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes controller registration pattern uses:\n- **ControllerDescriptor** as the registration metadata container\n- **InitFunc** as the factory function that creates and starts controllers\n- **ControllerContext** as the dependency injection container\n- **StartController()** as the orchestration function that handles initialization, feature gates, health checks, and debugging\n- **NewControllerDescriptors()** as the central registry where all controllers self-register\n\nThis design allows ~40+ controllers to be managed in a uniform, pluggable way with proper initialization ordering, feature gating, and lifecycle (`staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`): The base controller interface that requires:\\n- `Name()`: Returns the controller's canonical name\\n\\nOptional interfaces:\\n- to provide custom health checks for `/healthz` endpoint\\n\\n### Registration and Wiring Process\\n\\n**1. Central Discovery - NewControllerDescriptors()** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`): This function creates a map of all ~40 controller descriptors. Each controller registers itself by calling `register(newXControllerDescriptor())`. For example:\\n```\\nregister(newEndpointsControllerDescriptor())\\nregister(newDeploymentControllerDescriptor())\\nregister(newStatefulSetControllerDescriptor())\\n```\\n\\n**2. (controller.Interface, bool, error) {\\n    go endpointcontroller.NewEndpointController(\\n        ctx,\\n        controllerContext.InformerFactory.Core().V1().Pods(),\\n        controllerContext.InformerFactory.Core().V1().Services(),\\n        controllerContext.InformerFactory.Core().V1().Endpoints(),\\n        controllerContext.ClientBuilder.ClientOrDie(\\\"endpoint-controller\\\"),\\n        ...\\n    ).Run(ctx, workers)\\n    return nil, true, nil\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**4. Individual Startup - StartController()** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`): This function handles:\\n- Checking feature gates required by the controller\\n- Verifying the controller is enabled in configuration\\n- Applying startup jitter to prevent API server overload\\n- Calling the controller's InitFunc (which is the \\\"registration\\\" step)\\n- Mounting debug handlers if the controller implements `Debuggable`\\n- Registering health checks if the controller implements `HealthCheckable`\\n\\n**6. ControllerContext Dependency Injection** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`): All controllers receive a `ControllerContext` struct that provides:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: Access to Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: Access to cached resource watchers\\n- `ComponentConfig`: Controller-specific configuration\\n- `RESTMapper`: API resource discovery\\n- `ResyncPeriod`: Function that returns random sync periods (prevents thundering herd)\\n\\n**7. Actual Controller Implementation** (`pkg/controller/endpoint/endpoints_controller.go`): The concrete controller implements:\\n- Constructor (`NewEndpointController`) that registers event handlers on informers\\n- A `Run()` method that starts worker goroutines processing a work queue\\n- Event handlers that enqueue items when resources change\\n- Worker methods that process items and reconcile state\\n\\n### Reconciliation Loop\\n\\nThe manager's reconcile loop is implemented through:\\n1. **Event-driven queueing**: Informers watch for resource changes and trigger event handlers\\n2. **Work queue**: Items are added to a rate-limited work queue\\n3. **Worker goroutines**: Multiple workers process items from the queue\\n4. **Reconciliation**: Each worker item triggers comparison and reconciliation of desired vs actual state\\n5. **Retries**: Failed items are re-queued with exponential backoff\\n\\n### Leader Election Integration\\n\\nControllers are registered and started within a leader election context. Only the leader node runs the controllers, ensuring single-writer semantics. The `Run()` function in `controllermanager.go` uses `leaderElectAndRun()` to gate controller startup on leader election.\\n\\n### Key Differences from controller-runtime\\n\\nWhile the task mentions controller-runtime patterns (Reconciler interface, SetupWithManager), Kubernetes controllers use its own patterns:\\n- Instead of `SetupWithManager()`, Kubernetes uses the `InitFunc` approach\\n- Instead of a single `Reconcile()` method, Kubernetes controllers implement `Run()` methods with work queues\\n- Instead of manager auto-wiring, Kubernetes manually creates and passes clients/informers via `ControllerContext`\\n\\nThe patterns are semantically equivalent but architecturally different, with Kubernetes' approach being lower-level and more explicit about resource management.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4580,"cache_read_input_tokens":61503,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4580},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7e424aad-fdc6-45de-b667-24cea002e3ec","uuid":"28134636-285d-4f4e-a04c-04206c055dfa"}

ControllerContext Dependency Injection** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`): All controllers receive a `ControllerContext` struct that provides:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: Access to Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: Access to cached resource watchers\\n- `ComponentConfig`: Controller-specific configuration\\n- `RESTMapper`: API resource discovery\\n- `ResyncPeriod`: Function that returns random sync periods (prevents thundering herd)\\n\\n**7. Actual Controller Implementation** (`pkg/controller/endpoint/endpoints_controller.go`): The concrete controller implements:\\n- Constructor (`NewEndpointController`) that registers event handlers on informers\\n- A `Run()` method that starts worker goroutines processing a work queue\\n- Event handlers that enqueue items when resources change\\n- Worker methods that process items and reconcile state\\n\\n### Reconciliation Loop\\n\\nThe manager's reconcile loop is implemented through:\\n1. **Event-driven queueing**: Informers watch for resource changes and trigger event handlers\\n2. **Work queue**: Items are added to a rate-limited work queue\\n3. **Worker goroutines**: Multiple workers process items from the queue\\n4. **Reconciliation**: Each worker item triggers comparison and reconciliation of desired vs actual state\\n5. **Retries**: Failed items are re-queued with exponential backoff\\n\\n### Leader Election Integration\\n\\nControllers are registered and started within a leader election context. Only the leader node runs the controllers, ensuring single-writer semantics. The `Run()` function in `controllermanager.go` uses `leaderElectAndRun()` to gate controller startup on leader election.\\n\\n### Key Differences from controller-runtime\\n\\nWhile the task mentions controller-runtime patterns (Reconciler interface, SetupWithManager), Kubernetes controllers use its own patterns:\\n- Instead of `SetupWithManager()`, Kubernetes uses the `InitFunc` approach\\n- Instead of a single `Reconcile()` method, Kubernetes controllers implement `Run()` methods with work queues\\n- Instead of manager auto-wiring, Kubernetes manually creates and passes clients/informers via `ControllerContext`\\n\\nThe patterns are semantically equivalent but architecturally different, with Kubernetes' approach being lower-level and more explicit about resource management.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
